# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0`

# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` with my findings about controller registration in kubernetes/kubernetes.

## Summary

I traced how controllers register themselves with the manager in kubernetes/kubernetes and found:

### Key Components:

1. **Controller Interface** (`staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`)
   - Base `Interface` with `Name()` method
   - Optional `Debuggable` and `HealthCheckable` interfaces

2. **Controller Manager Context** (`staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go`)
   - Acts as the "manager" providing shared resources
   - Provides informer factories, client builders, and REST mappers
   - Coordinates controller lifecycle through `Stop` channel and `InformersStarted` signal

3. **Reconciler Pattern**
   - Multiple implementations across the codebase (plugin manager, volume manager, endpoint reconciliation)
   - Defines `Reconciler` interfaces with `Run()` methods for periodic reconciliation loops

4. **Sample Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/`)
   - Demonstrates the standard registration pattern
   - Controllers accept a `ControllerContext`, set up informer event handlers, and implement a `Run()` method
   - Main reconciliation happens in `syncHandler()` methods

5. **Main Controller Manager** (`cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go`)
   - Orchestrates starting multiple controllers
   - Creates `ControllerContext` with shared resources
   - Handles leader election for HA deployments

The registration pattern in kubernetes/kubernetes differs from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime's `SetupWithManager()` approach, using instead a simpler pattern where the manager provides a context containing shared informers and clients, and con
... (truncated)

registration follows a structured pattern distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime. Controllers in kubernetes/kubernetes are registered and managed through a manager pattern that uses shared informer factories and a controller context.\\n\\n## Key Registration Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface Definition\\nThe base `Interface` type is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`. This interface defines the minimal contract for a controller with a `Name()` method. Controllers can optionally implement the `Debuggable` interface (providing debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (providing health checks).\\n\\n### 2. Controller Manager Context\\nThe `ControllerContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go` acts as the manager, providing:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: for sharing informers across controllers\\n- `ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory`: for generic controller access\\n- `RESTMapper`: for REST resource mapping\\n- `Stop` channel: for graceful shutdown\\n- `InformersStarted` signal: for controller synchronization\\n\\n### 3. Reconciler Patterns\\nMultiple reconciler implementations demonstrate the reconciliation loop pattern:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/reconciler/reconciler.go` defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Run()` method\\n- `pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/reconciler/reconciler.go` implements reconciliation for volume attach/detach\\n- `pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go` defines `EndpointReconciler` for managing API server endpoints\\n\\nThese reconcilers run periodic loops that reconcile desired state with actual state.\\n\\n### 4. Sample Controller Registration Flow\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/` demonstrates the standard pattern:\\n\\n**Initialization** (`main.go`):\\n1. Create informer factories: `kubeinformers.NewSharedInformerFactory()` and custom informer factories\\n2. Create the controller: `NewController(ctx, kubeClient, exampleClient, informers...)`\\n3. Start informer factories: `kubeInformerFactory.Start(ctx.Done())`\\n4. Run the controller: `controller.Run(ctx, workerCount)`\\n\\n**Controller Structure** (`controller.go`):\\n- `NewController()` initializes the Controller struct with clients, listers, and work queue\\n- Sets up event handlers on informers to queue work items when resources change\\n- `Run()` method waits for cache sync, then starts worker goroutines\\n- `syncHandler()` is the main reconciliation method that compares desired vs actual state\\n\\n### 5. Main Controller Manager\\nThe `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` file implements the main entry point that:\\n1. Creates a `ControllerContext` with shared informers and clients\\n2. Orchestrates starting multiple controllers in the manager\\n3. Uses `leader election` for HA setups\\n4. Manages the lifecycle of all controllers through the main `Run()` function\\n\\n## Registration Summary\\n\\nUnlike sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime which uses a `SetupWithManager()` pattern, Kubernetes controllers register themselves by:\\n1. Implementing the `Interface` interface with a `Name()` method\\n2. Accepting a `ControllerContext` containing shared resources (informers, clients)\\n3. Implementing a `Run(ctx context.Context, ...)` method that starts the reconciliation loop\\n4. Setting up event handlers on informers to populate a work queue\\n5. Processing items from the work queue in worker goroutines, calling the sync handler\\n\\nThe manager (embodied by the controller manager process and the ControllerContext) is responsible for:\\n- Creating and configuring shared informer factories\\n- Providing clients and REST mappers to controllers\\n- Coordinating informer startup and controller initialization\\n- Managing graceful shutdown through context cancellation\\n- Handling leader election for HA deployments\"\n}\n",

registration follows a structured pattern distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime. Controllers in kubernetes/kubernetes are registered and managed through a manager pattern that uses shared informer factories and a controller context.\\n\\n## Key Registration Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface Definition\\nThe base `Interface` type is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`. This interface defines the minimal contract for a controller with a `Name()` method. Controllers can optionally implement the `Debuggable` interface (providing debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (providing health checks).\\n\\n### 2. Controller Manager Context\\nThe `ControllerContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go` acts as the manager, providing:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: for sharing informers across controllers\\n- `ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory`: for generic controller access\\n- `RESTMapper`: for REST resource mapping\\n- `Stop` channel: for graceful shutdown\\n- `InformersStarted` signal: for controller synchronization\\n\\n### 3. Reconciler Patterns\\nMultiple reconciler implementations demonstrate the reconciliation loop pattern:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/reconciler/reconciler.go` defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Run()` method\\n- `pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/reconciler/reconciler.go` implements reconciliation for volume attach/detach\\n- `pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go` defines `EndpointReconciler` for managing API server endpoints\\n\\nThese reconcilers run periodic loops that reconcile desired state with actual state.\\n\\n### 4. Sample Controller Registration Flow\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/` demonstrates the standard pattern:\\n\\n**Initialization** (`main.go`):\\n1. Create informer factories: `kubeinformers.NewSharedInformerFactory()` and custom informer factories\\n2. Create the controller: `NewController(ctx, kubeClient, exampleClient, informers...)`\\n3. Start informer factories: `kubeInformerFactory.Start(ctx.Done())`\\n4. Run the controller: `controller.Run(ctx, workerCount)`\\n\\n**Controller Structure** (`controller.go`):\\n- `NewController()` initializes the Controller struct with clients, listers, and work queue\\n- Sets up event handlers on informers to queue work items when resources change\\n- `Run()` method waits for cache sync, then starts worker goroutines\\n- `syncHandler()` is the main reconciliation method that compares desired vs actual state\\n\\n### 5. Main Controller Manager\\nThe `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` file implements the main entry point that:\\n1. Creates a `ControllerContext` with shared informers and clients\\n2. Orchestrates starting multiple controllers in the manager\\n3. Uses `leader election` for HA setups\\n4. Manages the lifecycle of all controllers through the main `Run()` function\\n\\n## Registration Summary\\n\\nUnlike sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime which uses a `SetupWithManager()` pattern, Kubernetes controllers register themselves by:\\n1. Implementing the `Interface` interface with a `Name()` method\\n2. Accepting a `ControllerContext` containing shared resources (informers, clients)\\n3. Implementing a `Run(ctx context.Context, ...)` method that starts the reconciliation loop\\n4. Setting up event handlers on informers to populate a work queue\\n5. Processing items from the work queue in worker goroutines, calling the sync handler\\n\\nThe manager (embodied by the controller manager process and the ControllerContext) is responsible for:\\n- Creating and configuring shared informer factories\\n- Providing clients and REST mappers to controllers\\n- Coordinating informer startup and controller initialization\\n- Managing graceful shutdown through context cancellation\\n- Handling leader election for HA deployments\"\n}\n",
